                                                       STRUCTURE OF DATA IN CORE 

General Comments 

HSPF makes use of a single, large Common block (called SCRTCH) to store data in the machine's memory. The various modules in HSPF each have their own version of this block, so that the arrangement of data in SCRTCH can be tailored to their individual needs.  For example,  The application modules PERLND, IMPLND and RCHRES all use the first part of SCRTCH to store their respective parameters, state variables and computed fluxes, while the latter part is used to hold time series (input and computed). On the other hand, the Run Interpreter does not deal with time series, so uses the latter part of SCRTCH to store the various tables which it uses to process the User's Control Input. 

There are, thus, many different versions of Common block SCRTCH in HSPF, each with its own arrangement of variables and arrays. 

The data structures for the operating modules such as PERLND, IMPLND and RCHRES, are called "Operation Status Vectors" (OSV) because  they contain all the information (parameters, state variables) needed to describe the status of an operation and, hence, to restart  it after an interruption. 

HSPF has been designed so that, when a module such as PERLND is temporarily interrupted to permit some other module to perform its  work, the OSV in SCRTCH is copied to disc so that it can be copied back when PERLND resumes execution. Meanwhile, the other module  (say RCHRES) uses SCRTCH to store its OSV, and also copies the contents to disc when it is interrupted and PERLND resumes work.  

           
Conventions Used in Data Structures  
           
The datasets which document the structure of data in core contain the following information: 

1.   The arrangement (sequence) of variables in SCRTCH, including names used for groups of data items. This is documented in the 
column headed "Identifier Structure".  The system used is similar to that used to denote a "structure" or "tree" of data in the PL/1 computer language.  Each name has a "level" associated with it.  The highest level is 1 and subsequent numbers  denote progressively lower levels.  If a name is a group name, it is followed by the set of names which it includes, all of which are of subordinate level to it.  This system provides for the nesting of data to any desired level.  For example, in dataset DATSTR1, OSVPER includes all the other names in the structure and is, thus, the name of the entire OSV.  "Flag and  Pointers" includes ASVEC, AGFG, etc. and ASVEC includes AIRTFG, SNOWFG, etc.  Since Fortran does not include the use of  data "structures", we implement these data overlays using the EQUIVALENCE statement.  For example, ASVEC(1) and AIRTFG are equivalenced, so that we can use the name ASVEC if we want to refer to the entire group of 12 flags, but use the name AIRTFG or SNOWFG, etc. if we are dealing with one individual flag.  HSPF makes extensive use of this method for simulating data structures.  
           
2.   The "Type" of the variable:  
I4   for  4-byte integer 
R4   for  4-byte real  
R8   for  8-byte real (double precision) 
Where this designation is followed by "-C", it indicates that the variable is used to store characters, not numbers.

3.   The function of each variable.  This is a short description of what it represents.  

4.   The "kind" of each variable, where applicable.  Point-valued time series are denoted by "*" and mean-valued time series by  "-".
(See Appendix III in the User's Manual for a discussion of point- and mean-valued time series). 

5.   The internal and external units and default/initial values in the Metric and English systems (where applicable). The "internal units" are those with which the HSPF code deals internally.  The "external units" are those with which it deals externally; that is, the units in which the User's Control Input is supplied and in which the system expects input time series to be expressed and in which it reports results or outputs time series.  The "units" fields are blank for  quantities which do not have dimensions (eg. flags, fractions).  The default/initial value field contains the default values for parameters and the default initial values for state variables.  If these values can be over-ridden by the user, they appear in the "External" columns; if the user has no control over them they appear in the "Internal" columns.  For a flag, the value OFF means zero; ON means a non-zero value, usually 1.  The default/initial value fields are blank if there is no default/initial value. 
           
6.   Units are expressed as follows:
     (1)  Every basic unit is represented by a standard abbreviation eg. mm for millimeter
     (2)  The units of each quantity are expressed as:
                   <product of basic units>/<product of basic units>
          where <product of basic units> is
                 basic unitU. basic unite
                 eg  mm.kg.sec
          (No periods are used in standard abbreviations to avoid confusion with multiplication symbol)
     (3)  Exponents on basic units are indicated by a numeric suffix eg. mm2 for square millimeters.
     (4)  For Metric units, we use the standard prefixes to indicate units which differ by powers of ten, e.g.
                          u for micro
                          m for milli
                          k for kilo
                          M for million
          To avoid ambiguity, we sometimes use parentheses, e.g.
                        (km)2 means square kilometers
                        k(m2) means thousands of sq. meters

 2 PQUAL 

************************************************************************************** 
  Note: In this section of the OSV the following symbols are used: 

    QUAL    means a quality constituent  

    QUALSD  means a quality constituent whose removal from the land  
            surface is simulated by association with sediment washoff  
            and scour  
 
    QUALOF  means a quality constituent which is simulated as follows:   
            (a) accumulation and removal, irrespective of runoff   
                intensity, as specified by parameters ACQOPM(12,*) and   
                REMQOM(12,*)   
            (b) washoff by surface runoff of water   
 
    QUALIF  means a quality constituent simulated in interflow   
 
    QUALGW  means a quality constituent simulated in groundwater   
 
    Any QUAL may be handled using any combination of the above approaches.   
 
    ZQ      means the maximum number of QUAL's which can be handled in one operation     (10)  
    ZQSD    means the maximum number of QUALSD's which can be handled in one operation   (10)  
    ZQOF    means the maximum number of QUALOF's which can be handled in one operation   (10)  
    ZQIF    means the maximum number of QUALIF's which can be handled in one operation   (10)  
    ZQGW    means the maximum number of QUALGW's which can be handled in one operation   (10)  
**************************************************************************************

                                            Operation Status Vector for the Impervious 
                                                  Land-Segment Application Module  
                                                             (IMPLND)

            abbreviated "ILS"  
        2.  OSV for module sections ATEMP and SNOW are identical 
            to those in module PERLND -- refer to OSV for PERLND 
            for those sections.

  3 Parameters 

   4 Flags and pointers

     6 AIRTFG            1 I4   for ATEMP                                                                      OFF            OFF

     6 IWATFG            3 I4   for IWATER                                                                     OFF            OFF  
     6 SLDFG             4 I4   for SOLIDS                                                                     OFF            OFF  
     6 IWGFG             5 I4   for IWTGAS                                                                     OFF            OFF  
     6 IQALFG            6 I4   for IQUAL                                                                      OFF            OFF  

    5 PFLAG(6)          14 I4   printout level flags for each                                                  4              4  
                                section. Same code as for IMPPFG 
    5 PIVL              26 I4   no. of simulation intervals in                                                 1              1  
                                PIVL level printout (only  
                                effective if IMPP=2) 
    5 PYREND            27 I4   the last calendar month in the                                                 9              9  
                                "printout year"  
    5 IMPPFG            28 I4   printout level flag for ILS as a 
                                whole: 
                                2 means every PIVL intervals 
                                3 means every day  
                                4 means every month  
                                5 means every printout year  
                                6 means never  

    5 UNIT(5)           29 I4   unit systems and Fortran unit nos  
                                for printing

                                UCI and for internal work:                                                     1              1  
                                1 means English system 
                                2 means Metric system

                                input of time series (eg. from 
                                disc files)  Same values as UUNITS.                                            1              1  
     6 OUNITS           31 I4   indicates system of units used for 
                                output of time series (eg. to disc 
                                files)  Same values as UUNITS.                                                 1              1  
     6 PUNIT(2)         32 I4   if PUNIT(1)> 0, printout in                                                    0              0  
                                English units is required.  Value  
                                is the FORTRAN unit no. to be used 
                                if PUNIT(2)> 0, printout in metric                                             0              0  
                                units is required.  Value is the 
                                FORTRAN unit no. to be used

 2 IQUAL 

************************************************************************************** 
  Note: In this section of the OSV the following symbols are used: 

    QUAL    means a quality constituent  

    QUALSD  means a quality constituent whose removal from the land  
            surface is simulated by association with solids washoff  

    QUALOF  means a quality constituent which is simulated as follows: 
            (a) accumulation and removal, irrespective of runoff 
                intensity, as specified by parameters ACQOPM(12,ZQOF)  
                and REMQOM(12,ZQOF)  
            (b) washoff by surface runoff of water 

    Any QUAL may be handled using any combination of the above approaches. 

    ZQ      means the maximum number of QUAL's which can be handled in one operation 
    ZQSD    means the maximum number of QUALSD's which can be handled in one operation 
    ZQOF    means the maximum number of QUALOF's which can be handled in one operation 
**************************************************************************************
